  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a92c635f-bf04-47c1-844f-d796f397272a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer14264907718954695120">Dorina Basarab is a dhampir-half human, half vampire. Subject to uncontrollable rages, most dhampirs live very short, very violent lives.   <span id="freeText14264907718954695120" style="display:none">Dorina Basarab is a dhampir-half human, half vampire. Subject to uncontrollable rages, most dhampirs live very short, very violent lives. So far Dory has managed to maintain her sanity by unleashing her anger on those demons and vampires who deserve killing.<br /><br />Now Dory's vampire father has come back into her life. Her Uncle Dracula (yes, <i>the</i> Dracula), infamous even among vampires for his cruelty and murderous ways, has escaped his prison. And her father wants Dory to work with gorgeous master vampire Louis-Cesare to put him back there.<br /><br />Vampires and dhampirs are mortal enemies, and Dory prefers to work alone. But Dracula is the only thing on Earth that truly scares her, so when Dory has to go up against him, she'll take all the help she can get… ...</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_145896395" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/145896395" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/145896395?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2011">reviewed-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=so-many-vampires">so-many-vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer145896395" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17550330862121019963">This book has led me to a very important decision: I’m going to learn to speak Romanian. It may take me a while, but I’m incredibly stubborn, and if I start now I can be fluent in a couple of years. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[My conscience informs me that I have to finish my research AND write my thesis first. Damn! <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/>Anyway, I want to learn Romanian just to be able to <s>whisper to Mircea in his native language when he visits me in my dreams</s> add it to my CV. It’s a beautiful language and I was al</span>
  <span id="freeText17550330862121019963" style="display:none">This book has led me to a very important decision: I’m going to learn to speak Romanian. It may take me a while, but I’m incredibly stubborn, and if I start now I can be fluent in a couple of years. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[My conscience informs me that I have to finish my research AND write my thesis first. Damn! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Anyway, I want to learn Romanian just to be able to <s>whisper to Mircea in his native language when he visits me in my dreams</s> add it to my CV. It’s a beautiful language and I was always interested in Romanian folklore. <br /><br />But let’s get back to the book. People who like the Cassie Palmer series will definitely love Dorina Basarab too. I, on the other hand, had the same problem with both: Karen Chance is a first level master at creating characters. You can’t help falling in love with Dorina, Louis-Cesare and even Radu (especially Radu!). But when it comes to building a story around those characters, she fails spectacularly every single time. I’ve read five of her books so far, and they all had the same problem. I’ll try to explain better. <br />I don’t like authors who underestimate their readers. It happens more often than not, authors treating their audience like a bunch of idiots, explaining everything about a dozen times while keeping those sentences short and simple just in case. But Karen Chance does exactly the opposite: she overestimates <b>herself</b>. She writes every book like it’s her last, trying to put too much content into it. It’s especially evident in action scenes: too much is happening at once and you just can't follow. What should be exciting ends up being utterly boring. But those characters keep you going, and because of them I WILL read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6203049.Death_s_Mistress__Dorina_Basarab___2_" title="Death's Mistress (Dorina Basarab, #2) by Karen Chance" rel="nofollow noopener">Death's Mistress</a>, even if I wasn’t planning to at first. I just have to find out how things work out for everyone!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17550330862121019963" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15052124126124009018">I love love love this book! <br/>This is a great story for people who love urban fantasy. It's action packed, fast paced and the plot is well thought out. Plus it has a lot of wit and sarcasm, which makes it a typical Karen Chance book. She has the wonderful ability of getting you soaked up in a fantasy world with a variety of creatures and serious problems, but still she keeps a funny edge, never taking herself too seriously. The inclusion of characters like Olga (hilarious), Radu (you can't help bu</span>
  <span id="freeText15052124126124009018" style="display:none">I love love love this book! <br />This is a great story for people who love urban fantasy. It's action packed, fast paced and the plot is well thought out. Plus it has a lot of wit and sarcasm, which makes it a typical Karen Chance book. She has the wonderful ability of getting you soaked up in a fantasy world with a variety of creatures and serious problems, but still she keeps a funny edge, never taking herself too seriously. The inclusion of characters like Olga (hilarious), Radu (you can't help but love the guy) and "Stinky" (no comment needed...) make sure of that too. <br /><br />I also loved the tension between Louis-Cesare and Dory. It is present throughout the whole book (and ranging from hate to attraction) but it doens't take over the story line. I can't wait to see where Karen Chance plans to take their relationship. <br /><br />I read Midnight's Daughter before the Cassie Palmer series so I've always loved Mircea cause he is more fleshed out in this book. However manipulative he has a strange affection for his family members and refuses to be pushed away by Dory. <br /><br />I've read and reread this book with much pleasure and I can't wait for the next installment (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6203049.Death_s_Mistress__Dorina_Basarab___2_" title="Death's Mistress (Dorina Basarab, #2) by Karen Chance" rel="nofollow noopener">Death's Mistress</a> out January 2010) .</span>

<div id="review_167763753" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167763753" />
    <a title="VampireNovelFan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4897902-vampirenovelfan"><img alt="VampireNovelFan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1296445543p2/4897902.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167763753?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="VampireNovelFan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="VampireNovelFan" href="/user/show/4897902-vampirenovelfan">VampireNovelFan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781400167388" href="/book/show/8065084-midnight-s-daughter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=shifters">shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=fae">fae</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167763753" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8459748368918046878"><a href='http://vampirenovelfan.wordpress.com/2012/09/16/midnights-daughter-dorina-basarab-1-my-socks-have-been-rocked/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <b>My socks have been rocked!</b>
</a><br/><br/> 
  <em>
    <strong>""I ran out of stock around midnight and dropped by a place, got some Chinese." I hoped he meant takeout...."Mu-shu pork" he told me indignantly."</strong>
  </em>
 <br/><br/>I held off from immediately jumping into the Dorina Basarb series, a spin-off of the Cassie Palmer novels by Karen Chance, for a couple of reasons:<br/><br/>1)I have some quirks with the Cassie Palmer books that I feared could spill over into this series<br/><br/>and<br/><br/>2)I wasn't sure if I wanted to invest in a series with such a l</span>
  <span id="freeText8459748368918046878" style="display:none"><a href="http://vampirenovelfan.wordpress.com/2012/09/16/midnights-daughter-dorina-basarab-1-my-socks-have-been-rocked/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>My socks have been rocked!</b>
</a><br /><br /> 
  <em>
    <strong>""I ran out of stock around midnight and dropped by a place, got some Chinese." I hoped he meant takeout...."Mu-shu pork" he told me indignantly."</strong>
  </em>
 <br /><br />I held off from immediately jumping into the Dorina Basarb series, a spin-off of the Cassie Palmer novels by Karen Chance, for a couple of reasons:<br /><br />1)I have some quirks with the Cassie Palmer books that I feared could spill over into this series<br /><br />and<br /><br />2)I wasn't sure if I wanted to invest in a series with such a long wait between novels. In my perfect world, I'd get two books per year when it comes to my fave series, not one every TWO years.<br /><br />So it took quite a while to get around to this, but I am so glad I finally did.<br /><br />This spin-off series centers around Dorina Basarab, a dhampir (vampire/human hybrid) assassin. Not quite enough of either species, Dorina's kind is rare and doesn't fit anywhere in either society. It doesn't help that she is subject to rages that cause her to black out and endanger not only those around her, but herself as well.<br /><br />It turns out she is the daughter of the great and powerful Mircea Basarab, and he needs her skills to help capture her uncle and his brother, Dracula, who has escaped from prison. Crazy and dangerous, this is a tall order, so Mircea also adds another master vampire to the mix, Louis-Cesare. The goal is for Dorina and Louis-Cesare to work together, but we all know the results when you try to mix oil and vinegar.<br /><br />This book was a lot of fun. This series has beaten the odds and has become an instant favorite, regardless of the lag time. It's missing my biggest annoyances with the Cassie books: an irritating love triangle and Cassie herself (I'm not just a fan, sorry). Dorina is much more likeable heroine for me. I laughed, I cried (okay, not really), I QUOTED!!<br /><br />Chance really knows how to write compelling and downright delicious male characters. Louis-Cesare has shot up on my list of book crushes. He's an amazing fighter, and the chemistry with Dorina is crazy good! It doesn't feel like your run of the mill relationship like with so many other novels. It's dynamic, it's got room to evolve, he isn't invisible, and Dorina actually can take care of herself quite well. It feels really natural, or about as natural as you can expect for supernaturals.<br /><br />Another pleasant surprise was Mircea. After reading the Cassie books we're only used to Mircea the lover and powerful Senate member. In these books we get to see Mircea the father. While we see the Senate member too, I really appreciate this perspective of him because it adds more depth to the character for me. I like him more and more because we see more of his vulnerability here as opposed to the Cassie books. When it comes to Dorina, you can tell that he doesn't have all of the answers, even when he tries to save face . It's a subtle chink in his armor and I love it!<br /><br />This is about as great of a start as one could hope for. I finished this book and couldn't wait to dive in to the next one! I think it's needless to say that I highly recommend this one.<br /><br />*Review also posted to <a href="http://www.amazon.com/review/R2UW6U5WU7EDFT" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8459748368918046878" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_233988941" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/233988941" />
    <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder"><img alt="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572373103p2/3048260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/233988941?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder">Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=a-own-book-form">a-own-book-form</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=part-of-series">part-of-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer233988941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15614144495393741433"><b>"I am sure there is a perfectly good reason why my niece is naked and tied to her bed. I am also equally certain that I do not wish to hear it"</b><br/><br/><br/>I've been reading the Cassie Palmer series for years but never had an urge to pick this side-series up. I've finally succumbed to temptation, probably because I had it on my shelf forever and it popped up as a group read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/55293' rel='nofollow noopener'>Girls, Guns and Grimoires</a>. While I liked the tone of Cassie's stories more, this one was also good in its own way.<br/><br/>It follows the st</span>
  <span id="freeText15614144495393741433" style="display:none"><b>"I am sure there is a perfectly good reason why my niece is naked and tied to her bed. I am also equally certain that I do not wish to hear it"</b><br /><br /><br />I've been reading the Cassie Palmer series for years but never had an urge to pick this side-series up. I've finally succumbed to temptation, probably because I had it on my shelf forever and it popped up as a group read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/55293" rel="nofollow noopener">Girls, Guns and Grimoires</a>. While I liked the tone of Cassie's stories more, this one was also good in its own way.<br /><br />It follows the standard fare with UF - Girl with powers who is tough and has a stick up the butt about certain issues. In this case Dory hates daddy dearest, the vampire Mircea from the Cassie series, vampires in general, most other supes, and...well, almost just people in general. She clearly doesn't have friends other than contacts she's willing to kill if things annoy her, with the exception of one who is currently missing. At first her attitude was abrasive and irritating, but she grows on me as her personality thaws when faced with other people she starts warming up to.<br /><br />Besides Mircea, Louis-Cesare is around from the Cassie series, but we see completely different sides of his personality here. At first he's an ass, then he's rather whiny, but then he's likable again. There is a disconnect with the vampire Mircea, a lack of warmth that shows some emotion at the end, and if it weren't for knowing his feelings in the Cassie series, I'd hate him along with Dory. For now I think there's a lot of emotion left to reveal and stuff he's holding back from his daughter.<br /><br />The world building is unique enough as it stays in the Cassie series but has Dory be a halfbreed between half vampire and half human, sometimes consumed with berserker rages that block her memory and bring out her violence. There's fae here too and for once I dig them - usually I find them irritating or too cruel, but I'm intrigued by the king and hope he comes up in the second book a few times. Yummy stuff.<br /><br />The story isn't too rich as it's mainly a hunt and fight kind of gig. Dory and Louis must work together and they don't actually solve much. Who they're looking for ends up on their doorstep in one way or another anyway and the fights mainly come to them. Dory isn't so badass that she doesn't get knocked around, and it didn't irritate me because this put in a touch of realism. <br /><br />Overall it was a decent Urban Fantasy opening. Characters are likable enough but I'm not hooked on any of them. The story was semi-strong but nothing that stands out in memory. Karen Chance writes well with dialogue and description and - while her Cassie series is overdone with too much action and not enough pause - here she calms down and dishes out normal sized servings of action between breaks.<br /><br />If you're a fan of the Cassie series, then definitely pick this one up for a try. You'll recognize some characters and style. If you're new to Karen Chance, I recommend picking up Cassie first, since it's more unusual and has a richer source of conflict for its first book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15614144495393741433" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1730766161" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1730766161" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14323468-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434090906p2/14323468.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1730766161?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/14323468-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=mine">mine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=gr2016">gr2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=heroines-i-love">heroines-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=books-i-love">books-i-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1730766161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7544791778893896144"><p>What an excellent first introduction to a UF series! </p> <blockquote>
  <i>Whatever control I may have acquired through long centuries of practice, I’m still a monster. And like the one who sired me, I’ll always love death and destruction a little bit more than anything, or anyone, else.</i>
</blockquote> <p>UF heroines are usually some of my favorite female characters ever written. And Dorina Basarab has definitely been added to this list. Dorina is a dhampir, half vampire and half human. Because of what she is, she’s been an outca</p></span>
  <span id="freeText7544791778893896144" style="display:none"><p>What an excellent first introduction to a UF series! </p> <blockquote>
  <i>Whatever control I may have acquired through long centuries of practice, I’m still a monster. And like the one who sired me, I’ll always love death and destruction a little bit more than anything, or anyone, else.</i>
</blockquote> <p>UF heroines are usually some of my favorite female characters ever written. And Dorina Basarab has definitely been added to this list. Dorina is a dhampir, half vampire and half human. Because of what she is, she’s been an outcast all her life as vampires hate dhampirs and humans fear her kind. Most dhampirs don’t have long life spans mostly because of their uncontrollable fits of rages, but Dorina has managed to build a life for herself, using her skills and her anger to kill vampires and demons who need killing. I loved Dorina! She’s got a ton of attitude, she’s snarky and kick-ass. </p> <p>She’s also the bastard daughter of Mircea, who is a very powerful vampire, which also makes her the niece of Dracula aka Vlad. Dorina and Mircea has quite a stormy relationship, he’s definitely not the best father, and Dorina kind of hates him. When Dorina’s best friend and roommate Claire goes missing and she’s unable to find any clues about who had taken her, she gets a little desperate. Which is why when Mircea asks her for her help in finding Dracula, who has escaped from his prison, and promises to help her find Claire, she’s unable to refuse. But she’s definitely not happy with the partner her father insist she works with, an arrogant and condescending vampire, Louis-Cesare. However, having fought against Uncle Dracula before, she knows she needs all the help she’s going to get. </p> <blockquote>
  <i> “Everything about you is provoking,” he breathed. “Your voice saying outrageous things, your body striding up and down, giving me orders, and your taste—”</i>
</blockquote> <p>Sparks flew between Dorina and Louis-Cesare, and I loved their banter and how both tried to be the one in charge of their mission. At first I didn’t like Louis-Cesare because of the way he looked down on Dorina, but after finding out about his horrible past I understood him better. It also helped that he changed towards Dorina the more he got to know her and her equally painful past. I loved the intense attraction between them, and I really hope there will be a romance for them in this series. </p> <p>The author created a wonderful and very interesting world with the fey, mages, demons, vampires, trolls and nulls. Claire is a null, which is a witch or wizard who can’t do magic but they can block out magical energy. I also really enjoyed the relationships between Dorina and her father, which is definitely very strained, but after how the book ended, I hope that things can change between them. The plot was also fast paced and full of action, which I enjoyed very much. </p> <p>I have not read her other series, Cassie Palmer, which I believe somehow ties in with this one, but I never felt lost while reading this book. </p> <p>This was a fantastic first installment and I loved it! I cannot wait to read the next book. Highly recommended to all UF fans.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="7544791778893896144" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer477209580" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13796980894923426915"><i>
  <blockquote>“Fresh blood at midnight isn't red. It's a purplish black that easily blends into the shadows.” </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>Karen Chance is my all-time most favorite <b>guilty pleasure</b>. Her stories are sinfully over-the-top. I. live. for. it. <br/><br/>Dorina Basabarb is a Dhampir, which comes with black out rages, family issues, and never feeling like she belongs. After endless years of existence, she has found a way to survive. Focus her fits on those preternatural beings that deserve death, and protect a magic null and Dory's be</span>
  <span id="freeText13796980894923426915" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>“Fresh blood at midnight isn't red. It's a purplish black that easily blends into the shadows.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Karen Chance is my all-time most favorite <b>guilty pleasure</b>. Her stories are sinfully over-the-top. I. live. for. it. <br /><br />Dorina Basabarb is a Dhampir, which comes with black out rages, family issues, and never feeling like she belongs. After endless years of existence, she has found a way to survive. Focus her fits on those preternatural beings that deserve death, and protect a magic null and Dory's best friend Claire. <br /><br />If there is one thing you should know about a Karen Chance novel, it is that the plot interlocks at least five different revolving forces at a time, creating a <b>larger than life, fast pace, survivalist adventure staring a bad-ass anti-hero. </b><br /><br />Claire is missing and Dorina is going crazy trying to hunt her down. Dory’s father comes back into her life to recruit her for a job. The job is to contain their deranged Uncle Dracula – yes, that Dracula. The payment for the job is simple; she will have the full force of the Vampire Senate hunting for Claire. <br /><br />Sinfully beautiful men? Check. Gory fight scenes? Check. Snark and banter and sass? Um, double-check. Characters which have real trauma, PTSD and emotional conflict from years of existence? Check and Check. <br /><br />The story could do with some editing because Karen Chance is lavish as hell. <br /><br />It’s sinfully decadent. </span>

<div id="review_2097653264" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2097653264" />
    <a title="Joana " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13984868-joana"><img alt="Joana " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352651892p2/13984868.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2097653264?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joana " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joana " href="/user/show/13984868-joana">Joana </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8176907-midnight-s-daughter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13984868-joana?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13984868-joana?shelf=i-dont-need-sleep-anyway-books">i-dont-need-sleep-anyway-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13984868-joana?shelf=laughed-out-loud">laughed-out-loud</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13984868-joana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13984868-joana?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2097653264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer58075938842379396">I can always rely on a good urban fantasy to make me excited to read again. This book was no exception. The only words I would really use to describe it are <b>fun and fast paced</b>. The reason the book really shined though, were the characters. <br/><br/>The story is centered around Dorina, our resident dhampir (half human/half vampire) with a whole slew of issues. Dhampirs in this world are a mostly hated and given their rarity, Dorina is quite the outcast. I've found that I really love stories where our main</span>
  <span id="freeText58075938842379396" style="display:none">I can always rely on a good urban fantasy to make me excited to read again. This book was no exception. The only words I would really use to describe it are <b>fun and fast paced</b>. The reason the book really shined though, were the characters. <br><br>The story is centered around Dorina, our resident dhampir (half human/half vampire) with a whole slew of issues. Dhampirs in this world are a mostly hated and given their rarity, Dorina is quite the outcast. I've found that I really love stories where our main character feels like an outsider because it creates a nice internal struggle that goes along nicely with the external ones. But that isn't to say that she spent the whole book wallowing in self-pity. In fact, she did the exact opposite. She takes no bullshit from anyone, and her i-give-no-fucks attitude was so fun to read about. She was physically and mentally able, which was a nice to surprise given that a lot of authors tend to forget about the mental strength. Her dedication to her best friend, Claire, was so great because I love seeing strong friendships in books. Her character was one of the best parts of this story and I definitely did not mind being stuck in her head.<br><br>Louis-Cesare, on the other hand, might have seemed like an ass in the beginning of the book, but his development was amazing. His prejudice against dhampirs was understandable and I like that he wasn't immeadiatly sold on Dorina because it allowed for a more organic and natural progression of their relationship. <br><br>Speaking of their relationship, I had no complaints whatsoever. It was a slow progression, with Dory and Louis-Cesare first hating and mistrusting eachother, which made for some amazing banter between the two of them. It developed into a grudging trust, and finally left of a note of will they or won't they. Their constant arguaments and stubborn personalities created the perfect amount of chemistry, and I couldn't be happier. They are definitely on my OTP list.<br><br>Another relationship that I loved was the one between Dory and her estranged father, Mircea. I loved the layers of complexity that were found there, and I really hope that the author decides to delve even deeper into this subject. Mircea was such a complex character and not without his faults, but Chance still managed to make him one of my favorite characters. I'm excited to see how Dory's and Mircea's realtionship will develop in future books. There's a mine of opportunity there, and I hope that Chance will take advantage of it.<br><br>Another honorable mention should also go out to Radu, the weird but lovable uncle, whose antics really served to lighten the mood. <br><br>The only complaint that I have for this book is the fact that, sometimes, the action scenes seemed a bit overfilled, in such a way that I found it hard to follow what was going on at times. Now, this might just have been me and my abilities of concentration (or lack thereof) but I found that I would have to reread certain parts in order to completely understand what had happened. <br><br>Also, please, whenever a character has the same name as another popular character *cough* Dory from Finding Nemo *cough*, try not to use it. It got distracting at one point, because everytime the name Dory was mentioned, I would picture this:<br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504173328ra/23730553.gif" width="200" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Again, this might just have annoyed me, so this wasn't such a big deal. <br> <br>To end on a positive note, I also would like to point out the humour in this book. I love when authors sneak in bits of humour in an otherwise dire situation. <br><br><i>"I'm not dead," I told her as distinctly as possible with the inside of my throat coated in dirt. <br> "Water," she gasped. "You need water."<br>I needed a two-month vacation on a beach, but water would do.</i><br> ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><i> Radu held up a hand. "I am sure there is a perfectly good reason why my niece is naked and tied to her bed. I am also equally certain that I do not wish to hear it."</i><br><br>All in all, this was a fantastic start to a new UF series, and I can't wait to dive into the other books!<br> _____________________________________________<br>WOW. DAMN. A NEW FAVORITE URBAN FANTASY SERIES. RTC.</span>

I highly recommend this book for urban fantasy lovers who love kick-ass chicks, sexy and dangerous vampires, a touch of romance, and action packed from beginning to end. Karen Chance is one of the most talented writers of urban fantasy right up there with Ilona Andrews and Jim Butcher......... Obviously, I love this book/series! :D<br/><br/>Awesome quotes:</span>
  <span id="freeText14364222454773797884" style="display:none">This is one of the best urban fantasy series and one of my most favorites. I love Dorina and Louis-Cesare. I always have a blast revisiting this world. I highly recommend this book for urban fantasy lovers who love kick-ass chicks, sexy and dangerous vampires, a touch of romance, and action packed from beginning to end. Karen Chance is one of the most talented writers of urban fantasy right up there with Ilona Andrews and Jim Butcher......... "I am sure there is a perfectly good reason why my niece is naked and tied to her bed. I am also equally certain that I do not wish to hear it."</i> <br /><br /><i>“Louis-Cesare’s anger suddenly filled the small room like water, and in a heartbeat his eyes went from silver tinged to as solid as two antique coins.<br />I sat frozen, awash in a sea of power. I guess he assumed the red hair would clue me in.”</i><br /><br /><i>“Louis-Cesare slowly pulled himself into a half-standing position against the side of the winery.'What?   <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/61253660" />

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer61253660" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14818435454216379464">More like a 3.5 star rating. I'm giving this 4 stars only because we can't give half a star ratings and 3 is too low. There is something about this and the Cassie Palmer series that just wears me out. I think it's too fast paced and too busy for me. Maybe if I were a slower reader and gave it more time to sink in but instead it just kind of wears on me. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_34544130" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34544130" />
    <a title="Julie (jjmachshev)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/882708-julie-jjmachshev"><img alt="Julie (jjmachshev)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1208126390p2/882708.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34544130?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie (jjmachshev)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie (jjmachshev)" href="/user/show/882708-julie-jjmachshev">Julie (jjmachshev)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/882708-julie-jjmachshev?shelf=2008-reads">2008-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34544130" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13031842709329402636">Very, very hard to review this book. I gobbled up Karen Chance's Cassie Palmer series and am anxiously awaiting book four to be released in April 2009. So I jumped on "Midnight's Daughter" which is an offshoot of that series. Technically, this is a standalone novel. But IMHO, you really should read about Cassie and that world before taking on Dorina. It provides a deeper insight into her world and events that have shaped the actions and intentions of some characters in her book.<br/><br/>Dorina is a dhamp</span>
  <span id="freeText13031842709329402636" style="display:none">Very, very hard to review this book. I gobbled up Karen Chance's Cassie Palmer series and am anxiously awaiting book four to be released in April 2009. So I jumped on "Midnight's Daughter" which is an offshoot of that series. Technically, this is a standalone novel. But IMHO, you really should read about Cassie and that world before taking on Dorina. It provides a deeper insight into her world and events that have shaped the actions and intentions of some characters in her book.<br /><br />Dorina is a dhampir, half human, half vamp, and has fits of uncontrollable rages like all dhampir. She's unusual in that she has managed to stay alive for over 500 years by channeling her rages into killing non-human creatures. When Daddy dearest shows up, Dorina knows it's not good news. When Daddy dearest asks her to go after Uncle Drac (yes, that Dracula!), she's sure he's only sending her on this suicide mission to finally be rid of her once and for all. Especially seeing the vamp he intends to be her partner...Louis-Cesare. It doesn't take long for both Dorina and Louis-Cesare to butt heads and become the targets of just about every other supernatural faction out there.<br /><br />Very complex. Very intense. Very dark. I sucked this down like a vamp with O negative. This is really a dark urban fantasy with heavy emotional and relationship threads. Just about every character in this book could use the services of a good shrink (I'm thinking Lynda Hilburn's Vampire Shrink) and you can forget about trying to predict what will happen next! I loved it. I want another Dorina book soon so I can see where she and maybe Louis too are headed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13031842709329402636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivie dan Glokta" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivie dan Glokta" href="/user/show/9838687-ivie-dan-glokta">Ivie dan Glokta</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer528911104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8109789690962158688">This is my second attempt to tackle down Chance's writing. I tried her Cassie Palmer series and got bored. Dorina Barsab followed closely in it's footsteps. <br/><br/>Chance invests great thought in her story, and it's evident. But i just couldn't keep my mind on the book. The more i read the more i found my mind wandering and focusing on things like; stuff i had to do around the house. Not many books out there get me to do my ironing, i'll tell you that.<br/><br/>So now, my ironing done and the book finished i am </span>
  <span id="freeText8109789690962158688" style="display:none">This is my second attempt to tackle down Chance's writing. I tried her Cassie Palmer series and got bored. Dorina Barsab followed closely in it's footsteps. <br /><br />Chance invests great thought in her story, and it's evident. But i just couldn't keep my mind on the book. The more i read the more i found my mind wandering and focusing on things like; stuff i had to do around the house. Not many books out there get me to do my ironing, i'll tell you that.<br /><br />So now, my ironing done and the book finished i am left unfulfilled. This story has left me indifferent.<br /><br />I don't know what went wrong and where precisely. Dorina has all the potential of being a great character but she doesn't deliver. She is not awesome, she is not horrible.....she just IS.<br /><br />There is only one aspect of this book that i found annoying and that would be how many people Chance dragged trough the sands of time. I mean it's not unusual in vampire novels to find a character that is a blast from the past but this was too much.<br /><br />Dracula, Casanova, Rasputin, Marlowe.... it just sounded pretentious. It was screaming- I took history class and remembered stuff!!!!<br /><br />I heard her books pick up, maybe i will try another down the line, but deffo not yet.<br /><br /><br /><br /> </span>

<div id="review_2694113904" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2694113904" />
    <a title="L. McCoy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60482096-l-mccoy"><img alt="L. McCoy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528161175p2/60482096.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2694113904?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="L. McCoy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="L. McCoy" href="/user/show/60482096-l-mccoy">L. McCoy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="MP3 CD 9781400187386" href="/book/show/9834842-midnight-s-daughter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60482096-l-mccoy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60482096-l-mccoy?shelf=hoopla">hoopla</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60482096-l-mccoy?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60482096-l-mccoy?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60482096-l-mccoy?shelf=so-boring-and-forever-taking">so-boring-and-forever-taking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60482096-l-mccoy?shelf=i-hope-my-worst-enemy-reads-this">i-hope-my-worst-enemy-reads-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60482096-l-mccoy?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2694113904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8158884376971718030">This is the 5th time in 2019 I’m giving a 1 star rating to something. It’s February. What the fuck?<br/><br/>What’s it about?<br/>Dorina has to find her missing roommate but in order to do so she’ll need help from a bunch of non-interesting characters to fight monsters and shit.<br/><br/>Why it gets 1 star:<br/>The story is not interesting. I’m not even sure what the hell this was, there’s so much terrible writing and boring ass filler.<br/>The characters... (sigh). They’re all either uninteresting or fully annoying. It doesn’t h</span>
  <span id="freeText8158884376971718030" style="display:none">This is the 5th time in 2019 I’m giving a 1 star rating to something. It’s February. What the fuck?<br /><br />What’s it about?<br />Dorina has to find her missing roommate but in order to do so she’ll need help from a bunch of non-interesting characters to fight monsters and shit.<br /><br />Why it gets 1 star:<br />The story is not interesting. I’m not even sure what the hell this was, there’s so much terrible writing and boring ass filler.<br />The characters... (sigh). They’re all either uninteresting or fully annoying. It doesn’t help that this book jumps into the story with barely any fucking background on anything, totally not what an author should do with the first book in a series.<br />This book is so damn boring. Most of this book is uninteresting people talking about uninteresting things because they’re uninteresting. There are a few action scenes but even they aren’t very well written. The book also drags things out way too much and I already mentioned the filler. Gosh... just writing this review and thinking about it makes me feel like I need a nap.<br />The romantic element is poorly done. Just very cheesy. The main thing that annoyed me is the author’s obsession with the word “sparks”. There were sparks here, sparks there, sparks almost everywhere. Oh and there was that drawn out sex scene that tries way too hard to be hot but isn’t.<br />This book is fairly predictable.<br />There’s some attempts at comic relief but they aren’t funny. There are a few unintentionally funny moments I suppose (example: Dorina is surprised to see a human or “norm” as she referred to him so all my brain could think is “NORMIE REEEEEEEE”) but yeah, this book can’t even do comic relief well.<br />The dialogue is pretty bad, then again I suppose annoying characters will mean annoying dialogue.<br />Where do I begin with the terrible writing? I already mentioned the dragging things out, filler and shitty dialogue. I already talked about the story just starting with no fucking background to make the reader care. Let’s see, ah here we go. The fact Chance couldn’t figure out if her main character is a Mary Sue is damsel in distress (either is annoying but for fuck’s sake at least don’t jump back and forth). Many scenes try too hard to be exciting (or in one case sexy) but aren’t. Oh, and the way that Louie Say-Zar’s (I don’t know how to spell his name, I listened to the audio edition, maybe it’s Caesar but I usually hear that pronounced as see-zur) full name is said every goddamn time he’s mentioned, like for fuck’s sake just call him Louie, no need to make every single mention of him an epic reveal of a name that doesn’t mean shit. Of course some lines, even outside of dialogue were dumb (“I’d have known blind folded that English isn’t his mother tongue.”) and lots of it is messy so it’s hard to tell what the fuck is going on.<br />The narration of the audio is not good. Between the bad voice attempts for the characters, the lack of emotion while reading (as in the tone of voice while reading a conversation at the dinner table and an action scene were the same) and the going from whispering to yelling at times, holy fuck...<br /><br />Overall:<br />This book is terrible, I’m surprised by the number of 4 and 5 star reviews I see here, I don’t understand that at all. I mean, I get that my opinion on books isn’t always the popular opinion but holy shit, this is a terrible book.<br />It’s boring as fuck, has annoying characters, is terribly written, full of bad dialogue and isn’t even well narrated.<br />Recommended if you need a nap, this book might at least make you fall asleep.<br /><br />1/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="8158884376971718030" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1107123061" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1107123061" />
    <a title="Jen Davis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis"><img alt="Jen Davis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548427639p2/4669344.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1107123061?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen Davis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen Davis" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis">Jen Davis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781440633447" href="/book/show/8600056-midnight-s-daughter">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1107123061" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11409793492664186452">Why, oh why, did I wait so long to pick up this book? I am a big fan of Karen Chance’s Cassie Palmer books and this is a spinoff from that series. It exists in the same world, featuring Mircea’s daughter Dory as the main protagonist. Simply put, it has all the awesome of the Cassie books without the headache from all that time travel.<br/><br/>Dory is a dhampir, a part human, part vampire hybrid. Her kind is rare and reviled by humans and vamps alike. She is nearly immortal and has super-senses… plus she </span>
  <span id="freeText11409793492664186452" style="display:none">Why, oh why, did I wait so long to pick up this book? I am a big fan of Karen Chance’s Cassie Palmer books and this is a spinoff from that series. It exists in the same world, featuring Mircea’s daughter Dory as the main protagonist. Simply put, it has all the awesome of the Cassie books without the headache from all that time travel.<br /><br />Dory is a dhampir, a part human, part vampire hybrid. Her kind is rare and reviled by humans and vamps alike. She is nearly immortal and has super-senses… plus she had a tendency to go into a berserker rage when pushed too far. Anyway, Dory hates her dad. She thinks he abandoned her as a child and never really cared about her. As an adult, she finds him heavy handed and wants nothing to do with him. Unfortunately, as this story begins, he comes to her with an offer she can’t refuse.<br /><br />Dory’s roommate is missing and she has been searching for her for a month. Mircea promises to use his considerable resources to bring Claire home IF Dory helps locate her crazed and revenge driven uncle, Vlad. Dory really wants to tell her dad to shove the job, but she puts her friend first and decides to accept. Coming along for the ride, is her other uncle’s progeny, Louis Cesare. (Cassie fans will recognize his backstory from those books.)<br /><br />At first, LC and Dory are like oil and water. But there is such a great dynamic there. He is so powerful and yet so vulnerable at the same time. Dory both rages against his strength at the same time she kind of revels in it. There is fantastic sexual tension, but as they really learn each other, I really believed there was more to it.<br /><br />Dory is a kick-ass heroine. She has some attitude, sure, but she is a good person and very loyal. She endures so much, yet she always comes out swinging. Then there is Louis Cesare. At first, he seems like he is a total douchebag, but the more I got to know him, the more I wanted to crawl inside of the book and give him a hug. OK. Maybe not just a hug, because WOAH he is hot.<br /><br />The plot is fantastic with breakneck pacing. I didn’t want to put it down! The world building is solid; and the character development is great too. There is so much action: fighting, plotting, double crossing, and violence. But just as prominent is time spent learning what makes these characters tick. I really cared about them and what would happen next.<br /><br />It’s really good Urban Fantasy with a perfect dose of romance peppered in. You don’t have to read the Cassie Palmer books to enjoy this, either, though you might understand a bit more about Mircea and LC if you do. — I can’t wait to read the next installment.<br /><br />Rating: A-</span>
  <a data-text-id="11409793492664186452" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_153651344" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/153651344" />
    <a title="Lynsey   (A Bookish Life)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5112089-lynsey-a-bookish-life"><img alt="Lynsey   (A Bookish Life)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499618776p2/5112089.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/153651344?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynsey   (A Bookish Life)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynsey   (A Bookish Life)" href="/user/show/5112089-lynsey-a-bookish-life">Lynsey   (A Bookish Life)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5112089-lynsey-a-bookish-life?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5112089-lynsey-a-bookish-life?shelf=the-holy-grail-of-book-series">the-holy-grail-of-book-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer153651344" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14272297446353546863">You know what's weird? Considering how many reviews I've written—especially this year after I set it as my New Year's Resolution to review every single book I read—what's weird is that most of my all-time <i>favourite </i>books don't even have a review at all because I read them waaaay before I discovered the joys of reviewing or having a virtual Goodreads bookshelf to keep a record of my books and ratings. So my favourites, like this one, just got slapped with an automatic 5-star rating based on hazy </span>
  <span id="freeText14272297446353546863" style="display:none">You know what's weird? Considering how many reviews I've written—especially this year after I set it as my New Year's Resolution to review every single book I read—what's weird is that most of my all-time <i>favourite </i>books don't even have a review at all because I read them waaaay before I discovered the joys of reviewing or having a virtual Goodreads bookshelf to keep a record of my books and ratings. So my favourites, like this one, just got slapped with an automatic 5-star rating based on hazy memories of awesomeness, and that was that.<br /><br />So, it's a bit sad that I am, then, to find that after my recent re-read of this book, 3 years and around 600 books after my first go, I find I can't in all honesty still give it 5 stars, so I've dropped it down to 4. I still really enjoyed it, don't get me wrong. But I'd be blind not to see that, although I love Chance's writing for its fast pacing and action-filled plots, a lot of it can be too chaotic and confusing with too much going on from too many directions and not enough exposition. For much of the book I was just waiting and hoping that any minute now I'd be told <i>why</i> Dory was doing what she was doing, or going where she was going, and who the heck are those people firing stuff at her now and why are they doing it?<br /><br />I imagine it all makes perfect sense in Karen Chance's head, but it doesn't always translate perfectly to her audience. It's kind of a double-edged sword, though, because the confusion is a side effect of having such intricate, complex, multi-layered, thought-provoking and detailed plots. She literally fits more plotting, world-building and characterisation into one page than some authors manage in three chapters (or whole books in the worst cases). But unless you're paying absolute, 100% focused attention (which admittedly I probably wasn't this time as I did the re-read as an audiobook) then you'll blink and miss something vital and be all "What the hell just happened?"<br /><br /><b>
  <u>But that's enough negativity!</u>
</b><br /><br />This is my favourite urban fantasy 'world' after all, (although I do prefer the main Cassandra Palmer series over this, the spin-off). So let's get on to what I still loved—The world, the setting, the magic, Dory, the real historical characters, Louis Cesare, the complex and strained relationships, Stinky, the sexual tension, the funny dialogue, Radu, the hot vamps, the hot smexy times, Dory's house that won't let her redecorate or move anything, the intelligent writing, Louis Cesare in a towel.<br /><br />That's quite a lot still to love, eh?<br /><br />Dory is a great main character. She has a bit of a bad attitude due to being a misfit and held in contempt by almost all supernatural factions AND humans, and she suffers rage episodes and has a dry, sarcastic sense of humour.<br /><br />Louis Cesare on the other hand is cool, suave, laconic, honourable and protective. They make a great fighting team, as long as Louis Cesare can keep up, and I look forward to re-visiting them in the next book, which I believe, if memory serves, is slightly less hectic than this one.<br /><br />Recommended to read after books 1&amp;2 of the Cassandra Palmer series.<br /><a href="http://www.karenchance.com/timeline.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Click here</a> for the series timeline.<br />4 Stars ★★★★</span>
  <a data-text-id="14272297446353546863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Chance's 'Cassandra Palmer' series</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer54868800" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5302919107966753699"><b>
  <i>Re-Read Review</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>First Read:</b> 2 Mar 2009 <b>Rating:</b> ✮✮✮✮✮<br/><b>Re-Read:</b> 10 Sept 2012 <b>Rating:</b> ✮✮✮✮✮<br/><br/><b>Midnight's Daughter</b> introduces us to Dorina Basarab. Think the name sounds familiar? That's because, if you have read Karen's <i>Cassandra Palmer</i> series, you've already met Dory's Daddy - Mircea Basarab. Dory's a dhampir - ½human, ½vamp - who experience uncontrollable rages and typically have a short live span. Dory, on the other hand, has lived for 500 yrs. <br/><br/>When Dory's best friend and roomie goes missing she g</span>
  <span id="freeText5302919107966753699" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Re-Read Review</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>First Read:</b> 2 Mar 2009 <b>Rating:</b> ✮✮✮✮✮<br /><b>Re-Read:</b> 10 Sept 2012 <b>Rating:</b> ✮✮✮✮✮<br /><br /><b>Midnight's Daughter</b> introduces us to Dorina Basarab. Think the name sounds familiar? That's because, if you have read Karen's <i>Cassandra Palmer</i> series, you've already met Dory's Daddy - Mircea Basarab. Dory's a dhampir - ½human, ½vamp - who experience uncontrollable rages and typically have a short live span. Dory, on the other hand, has lived for 500 yrs. <br /><br />When Dory's best friend and roomie goes missing she goes on the hunt to find out what's happened. Mircea approaches her with an offer she cannot refuse. For her help recapturing Uncle Drac he'll bring in help to find Claire. <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"London, 1889. Dark and stormy night. Ring any bells? I think the exact quote was, 'If you do not finish this tonight, if you leave him any avenue by which to return, I wash my hands of the whole affair. Next time, you will hunt him alone.'"</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> While Dory swore she'd never get involved again, she agrees because she's worried it may be the only way to get to Claire quickly enough. See, Claire has a special ability that makes her the interest of many. The one thing that Dory didn't count on was having to team up with Louis-Cesare, a <i>"judgmental, condescending, self-important son of a bitch"</i>. These two may start off with trust issues and a touch of disdain for each other, but during their mission that all changes. <br /><br />I LOVE this series. This re-read reminded me exactly why. In fact, I enjoy it slightly more than Chance's <i>Cassandra Palmer</i> series, which has a tendency to make me motion sick with all of the time traveling. Dory's a very strong-willed character with a soft center. I cannot wait to continue my series re-read in prep for the very long awaited third book in this series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12114440.Fury_s_Kiss__Dorina_Basarab___3_" title="Fury's Kiss (Dorina Basarab, #3) by Karen Chance" rel="nofollow noopener">Fury's Kiss</a> on 2 Oct. <br /><br />Of note: It is not necessary to read <i>Cassandra Palmer</i> before this series. Fans of this series may also find that series enjoyable and visa versa.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5302919107966753699" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_51101543" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/51101543" />
    <a title="Starfish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/128770-starfish"><img alt="Starfish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1238991646p2/128770.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/51101543?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Starfish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Starfish" href="/user/show/128770-starfish">Starfish</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer51101543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6078706451757264663">Atrocious. Really. Author cuts all sorts of corners, using black-outs and convenient memory dumps to garner sympathy for her main characters, while telling constantly. She also puts the entire novel in at high gear, but when all of Dorina's allies end up dead, she's got no weapons, is horribly injured and weak and has no options -- for the third time in short succession in the book -- well. You're less concerned, more, right then. Get on with it. <br/><br/>There were two things I liked about the book -- m</span>
  <span id="freeText6078706451757264663" style="display:none">Atrocious. Really. Author cuts all sorts of corners, using black-outs and convenient memory dumps to garner sympathy for her main characters, while telling constantly. She also puts the entire novel in at high gear, but when all of Dorina's allies end up dead, she's got no weapons, is horribly injured and weak and has no options -- for the third time in short succession in the book -- well. You're less concerned, more, right then. Get on with it. <br /><br />There were two things I liked about the book -- male lead goes off to sulk at the end of it, and Radu turned out to be surprisingly interesting. However, those couldn't make up for the rest of the book. Dorina is a collection of cliches thrown together without enough personality to make her something beyond them -- no, not even having aubergine hair helps, sorry. Dialogue that was supposed to be cutting and witty was just flat and unfunny. Writing was good except for some clumsy moments where it called attention to itself. The family politics which could have been interesting explored more fully got lost under a needlessly violent and confusing mash of Fey versus Dark Mage versus Good Vampires versus Rebel Vampires and Dracula thing -- an attempt to up and ante even further. I can't recommend this one at all. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6078706451757264663" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10340947667084826811" style="display:none">Dorina,half-vampire half-human and prone to dark rages,is on a mission.Her psycho Uncle Dracula has escaped from prison and her father wants Dorina to go and capture him with the help of fellow vampire Louis-Cesare.She likes to work alone but with Dracula to deal with,she is forced into the partnership.<br /> First,Louis-Cesare just bugged me,like a poor imitation of Jean-Claude from the Anita Blake series.The fighting with him and Dorina got boring very quickly as I hate this type of thing in my books.I like partners working together with quips and wit not her raging tantrums all the time about having to work with a partner. It was all a bit samey as the book went on and even the thought of seeing a new version of Uncle Dracula couldn't keep me interested.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11759746692897264577">4.5 stars: Love, love this new urban fantasy series!<br/><br/>This series has it all--high action, adventure, fantasy, mystery, a little romance--wow! Loved it--couldn't put it down. It is set in the same world as the Cassandra Palmer series by the same author. <br/><br/>The main character is strong, humorous, imperfect and likeable.   <span id="freeText11759746692897264577" style="display:none">4.5 stars: Love, love this new urban fantasy series!<br /><br />This series has it all--high action, adventure, fantasy, mystery, a little romance--wow! Loved it--couldn't put it down. It is set in the same world as the Cassandra Palmer series by the same author. <br /><br />The main character is strong, humorous, imperfect and likeable. She is a kick b*tt character, reminicent of Kate Daniels (another fav UF series). I also liked seeing more of Louis Ceasar and Micea who were in the other series. And I liked the hint of a romantic triangle between Dory, Louis Ceasar and the Fey King. <br /><br />There is a great short story in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/285212.On_the_Prowl__Alpha___Omega___0_5_" title="On the Prowl (Alpha &amp; Omega, #0.5) by Patricia Briggs" rel="nofollow noopener">On the Prowl</a> which should be read after this book and before <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6203049.Death_s_Mistress__Dorina_Basarab___2_" title="Death's Mistress (Dorina Basarab, #2) by Karen Chance" rel="nofollow noopener">Death's Mistress</a>. The short story is about Claire and occurs in time with the first book. Claire is Dory's missing friend who Dory is searching for in book one. The short story gives the details of what Claire is going through. Very good read. The short story collection is a good one--I also liked the Briggs and Wilks stories. Death's Mistress the next book in the series was downright fantastic. I liked it even better than Midnight's Daughter--non stop action with a lot of plot twists and turns.<br /><br />You don't have to read the Cassandra Palmer series before reading this one, but it would give you more backstory about some of the characters who appear in both series. Karen Chance is now on my 'must buy' list!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10549887719772446168">3.5 stars<br/><br/>Dory kicks ass, and she doesn't put up with shit from anyone especially those who think they are better than her. Since she's a dhampir, most people think they're better than her. Being Mircea's daughter has its benefits and complications. The benefits being part of a powerful vampire family.   <span id="freeText10549887719772446168" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />Dory kicks ass, and she doesn't put up with shit from anyone especially those who think they are better than her. Since she's a dhampir, most people think they're better than her. Being Mircea's daughter has its benefits and complications. The benefits being part of a powerful vampire family. However there are more complications mainly in the way of more enemies just because of who her family is. <br /><br />Dory was coerced into doing a large favor for Mircea. She was forced to work with Louis-Cesare, who has been in the Cassie Palmer series. He was an ass at first but grew on me. He and Dory are well matched in many ways. <br /><br />I decided to reread this since the 4th book in the series is finally coming out soon. It was a good thing that I did because there was a hell of a lot I couldn't remember. Many characters are in this and the Cassie Palmer series, but this has a completely different feel since Cassie and Dory aren't alike. The one thing that remains the same is the overly long action scenes. Sometimes I skim through them. Other than that it's an awesome book.<br /></span>

<div id="review_102488273" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102488273" />
    <a title="Suzanne (Under the Covers Book blog)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog"><img alt="Suzanne (Under the Covers Book blog)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583236251p2/3575839.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
